The Two Types of Power: Possible (Mumkina) and Facilitated (Muyassara)
Presenting Hanafi classification of obligatory power into possible and facilitated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between possible power (mumkina) and facilitated power (muyassara) and apply the Hanafi rules for obligation and qada' to each type.

Core Idea
Power as a condition of obligation is either ordinary ability (mumkina) or divine facilitation (muyassara), each with distinct legal consequences.

In Hanafi usul, the power required for an obligation is not monolithic. It is divided into two categories: possible power (al-qudra al-mumkina), which is the ordinary physical and instrumental ability, and facilitated power (al-qudra al-muyassara), a divine grace that makes obligation contingent on ease over time. Understanding this division is essential to correctly derive rulings for acts of worship—for example, why prayer and zakat have different conditions for obligation and qada'. This lesson unpacks this classification and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of conditional power
The passage opens by dividing 'conditional power' (al-qudra al-mashrūṭa) into two types: possible (mumkina) and facilitated (muyassara). Note that both are conditions for obligation, but they operate differently.
Conditional power means the obligation is contingent upon having this power; without it, the obligation does not arise.
2
Understand possible power (mumkina)
Possible power is defined as 'soundness of instruments and correctness of causes'—essentially having the physical ability and means. The author notes this is an interpretation by implication (tafsīr bil-lāzim), meaning it is a necessary consequence of true power.
This is the ordinary ability needed for acts like prayer: being in a state of purity, having the time, being physically capable.
3
Apply the rule for possible power
If the act is normally performed with this power and determination, the obligation is immediate (ʿaynan). If missed without negligence, qada' is required only if the act has a substitute (like prayer has a qada'). Negligence always incurs sin. However, if performance is not normally achievable (e.g., only a small part of the act can be done), then qada' is required.
The passage distinguishes between cases where the act is 'usually performed' (ghāliban) versus not. This affects whether qada' is due immediately or not.
4
Analyze the dispute with Zufar regarding the last part of time
For an act like prayer, if one only has power for part of the last time unit (e.g., can only pray 2 rak'as of a 4-rak'a prayer), the Hanafi view (against Zufar) holds the obligation exists. Zufar argued one must have power for the whole act; the Hanafis respond that the actual last moment is what matters, and extension is possible.
This is a key ikhtilaf illustrating how the definition of power affects obligation. The passage provides several dialectical arguments, ultimately preferring the Hanafi position.
5
Understand facilitated power (muyassara)
Facilitated power is a divine grace making obligation contingent on ease over time. The example is zakat: the obligation depends on the passing of a full year with surplus wealth. If the wealth is destroyed or debt interferes, the obligation drops because the condition of ease is no longer present.
This type of power is not about momentary ability but about the ease of duration. It explains why zakat is not required at every moment of the year.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة تقسيم القدرة إلى الممكنة والميسرة قسم الحنفية القدرة المشروطة، إلى ممكنة مفسرة بسلامة الألات وصحة الأسباب، وهو تفسير باللازم، وإلى ميسرة فاضلة عليها فضلاً منه تعالى باليسر، والأولى إن كان الفعل بها مع العزم غالباً فالواجب الأداء عينا، فإن فات بلا تقصير لم يأثم، ووجب القضاء إن كان له خلف، وإلا فلاقضاء ولا إثم، وإن قصر أثم مطلقاً، وإن لم يكن غالباً الأداء ليترتب القضاء كالأهلية في الجزء الأخير من الوقت وجب خلافاً لزفر رحمه الله تعالى لاعتباره قدر ما يحتمله وفي "التحرير" لأنه لاقطع بالأخير لإمكان الامتداد أقول: يلزم أن لا يقطع بالتضييق، وقد يقطع، وأيضاً الامتداد إما بازدياد الأجزاء، فيتسع ولانزاع فيه أو بالمد والبسط فيلزم بطلان القول بالجزء، وأيضا المناط الأخير الواقعى لا الأخير العلمى، فالأولى أن يقال: لاقطع بانقضاء الأخير لإمكان البقاء، وبطلان انطباق الكبير على مثل هذا الصغير ربما يمنع، وهذا كله جدل والحق القول بترتب القضاء، إما على نفس الوجوب، كما في النائم أو على وجوب جزء من الأداء، كما في النقل إذا فسد فتدبر وأما الثانية (القدرة الميسرة فيتقيد بها الوجوب، كالزكوة، فإنه شيئ قليل من كثير مرة بعد الحول مرة، ولهذا سقط بالهلاك وانتفى بالدين
Issue: Division of power into possible (mumkina) and facilitated (muyassara). The Hanafis divided conditional power into possible, interpreted as soundness of instruments and correctness of causes, and this is an interpretation by implication; and into facilitated, additional to it by a grace from Him (Exalted) by ease. The first: if the act is performed with it and with determination usually, then the obligation is to perform it as a specific duty, and if it is missed without negligence, he does not sin, and making up (qada') is required if it has a substitute, otherwise no qada' and no sin; and if he is negligent, he sins absolutely. And if performance is not usually achieved such that qada' would be required, like eligibility in the last part of time, it becomes obligatory, contrary to Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) because he considers the amount he can bear. In al-Tahrir: because there is no certainty about the last [moment] due to the possibility of extension. I say: this would necessitate not being certain about the narrowing, but there is certainty sometimes. Also, extension is either by increase of parts, so it expands and there is no dispute about that, or by extension and spreading, which would invalidate the statement of the part. Also, the criterion is the actual last, not the cognitive last. So it is better to say: there is no certainty about the expiry of the last due to the possibility of remaining, and the invalidity of applying the large to such a small one may be prevented. All of this is dialectic, and the truth is the statement requiring qada' either on the basis of the obligation itself, as in the case of a sleeping person, or on the basis of an obligation of a part of performance, as in the transfer when it is corruption, so ponder. As for the second (facilitated power), obligation is conditioned by it, like zakat, for it is a small thing from a large amount once after the year [passes] and once, and therefore it is dropped by destruction and removed by debt.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi classification of the power that is a condition of obligation (qudra shartiyya) into two types: possible (mumkina) and facilitated (muyassara). The possible power is interpreted as the soundness of limbs and instruments and the correctness of causes (e.g., being healthy, having the means). This is a necessary condition for obligations like prayer. The facilitated power is an additional divine grace that makes obligation contingent on ease, as in zakat, where the obligation depends on having wealth for a full year. The author then discusses the ruling for the first type: if one has this power and determines to perform the act, and it is usually the case that the act is done, then the obligation is to perform it immediately, and if it is missed without negligence, qada' is required if the act has a substitute (like prayer). If no substitute, no qada'. Negligence always incurs sin. A dispute with Zufar is mentioned regarding the last part of the time for prayer: Zufar held that if at the beginning of the last time one has power for only a part of the prayer, one is not obliged because one cannot complete the whole. The Hanafi view, based on the possibility of extension, obliges performance on the actual last moment, not the cognitive one. The author engages in a dialectical analysis, ultimately affirming qada' based on the obligation itself or an obligation of a part. The second type (facilitated power) is exemplified by zakat: obligation is tied to the ease of the year's passage, and if the wealth is destroyed or debt intervenes, the obligation falls away.

Key Terms
القدرة الممكنة (al-qudra al-mumkina): Power interpreted as soundness of instruments and causes; the ordinary ability required for most obligations.
القدرة الميسرة (al-qudra al-muyassara): A divine facilitation that makes obligation contingent on ease, e.g., in zakat, obligation depends on the annual cycle and surplus wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi division, in the case of zakat, what kind of power is relevant?
A) Possible power (mumkina) – the ability to pay at the moment.
B) Facilitated power (muyassara) – the grace of ease after a year.
C) Both equally.
D) Neither; zakat does not require any power.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of power into possible (mumkina) and facilitated (muyassara) determines when an obligation arises and whether qada' is required, with possible power tied to immediate ability and facilitated power to ease over time.

Hanafi Division of Capacity: Possible and Facilitated
Explains the Hanafi classification of capacity and its effect on obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between al-qudra al-mumkina and al-qudra al-muyassara, and apply the Hanafi rule that possible capacity obligates qada when performance is impossible, while facilitated capacity restricts obligation to ease.

Core Idea
Possible capacity makes every obligation binding; facilitated capacity ties obligation to ease.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, capacity (qudra) is a condition for obligation. The Hanafis uniquely divided capacity into two types to handle different kinds of obligations, from daily prayers to zakat. This lesson unpacks that division and shows how it determines whether a missed obligation must be made up (qada) or is waived entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of capacity
The text defines al-qudra al-mumkina (possible capacity) and al-qudra al-muyassara (facilitated capacity). Note the Arabic terms and their defining features.
Possible capacity is the minimum; facilitated capacity includes ease.
2
Understand the definition of possible capacity
It is explained by soundness of limbs and correctness of means. This is a necessary concomitant (lāzim) of capacity itself, not the essence.
This definition is used to attach rulings practically.
3
Apply the rule for possible capacity
If the act is generally possible with resolve, performance (adā') is obligatory. If missed without negligence, qada is required if there is a substitute; if with negligence, sin plus qada.
Three scenarios: with resolve, without resolve, with negligence.
4
Understand the special case: performance impossible but qada obligatory
When someone becomes responsible at the very end of the time (e.g., new Muslim, baligh, lunatic recovering), performance is impossible but qada is still obligatory. This is the Hanafi view against Zufar.
Obligation is transferred to qada because possible capacity existed at the moment of responsibility.
5
Understand facilitated capacity
This capacity ties obligation to ease, e.g., zakat: it requires growing wealth, free of debt, after a year. If ease is lost (wealth destroyed), obligation falls away.
Facilitated capacity lightens the burden; it is not strict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة تقسيم القدرة إلى الممكنة والميسرة قسم الحنفية القدرة المشروطة، إلى ممكنة مفسرة بسلامة الآلات وصحة الأسباب، وهو تفسير باللازم، وإلى ميسرة فاضلة عليها فضلاً منه تعالى باليسر، والأولى إن كان الفعل بها مع العزم غالباً فالواجب الأداء عينا، فإن فات بلا تقصير لم يأثم، ووجب القضاء إن كان له خلف، وإلا فلا قضاء ولا إثم، وإن قصر أثم مطلقاً، وإن لم يكن غالباً الأداء ليترتب القضاء كالأهلية في الجزء الأخير من الوقت وجب خلافاً لزفر رحمه الله تعالى لاعتباره قدر ما يحتمله وفي "التحرير" لأنه لا قطع بالأخير لإمكان الامتداد أقول: يلزم أن لا يقطع بالتضييق، وقد يقطع، وأيضاً الامتداد إما بازدياد الأجزاء، فيتسع ولا نزاع فيه أو بالمد والبسط فيلزم بطلان القول بالجزء، وأيضا المناط الأخير الواقعي لا الأخير العلمي، فالأولى أن يقال: لا قطع بانقضاء الأخير لإمكان البقاء، وبطلان انطباق الكبير على مثل هذا الصغير ربما يمنع، وهذا كله جدل والحق القول بترتب القضاء، إما على نفس الوجوب، كما في النائم أو على وجوب جزء من الأداء، كما في النقل إذا فسد فتدبر وأما الثانية القدرة الميسرة فيتقيد بها الوجوب، كالزكوة، فإنه شيء قليل من كثير مرة بعد الحول مرة، ولهذا سقط بالهلاك وانتفى بالدين قسم الحنفية القدرة التي هي شرط التكليف إلى ممكنة وميسرة . ١ - فالقدرة الممكنة مفسرة بسلامة الآلات وصحة الأسباب، وهو تفسير باللازم لأنها أدنى ما يتمكن به المأمور من أداء المأمور به بدنياً كان أو مالياً، ولا شك أن سلامة الآلات وصحة الأسباب لازمة للقدرة، ودليل لوجودها فأقيمت مقامها في تعلق الأحكام. من المكلف -٢ والقدرة الميسرة : هي التي يتمكن بها العبد من الفعل مع اليسر، كالقدرة المشروطة في إيجاب الزكاة، من المال النامي الفاضل عن الحوائج الأصلية، الذي حال عليه الحول شرط الله فيها زيادة اليسر فضلاً منه تعالى على عباده باليسر، والقدرة الأولى الممكنة شرط لأداء كل واجب، لكن إن كان إتيان الفعل بسبب هذه القدرة مع العزم وإرادة الفعل في غالب ظنه، فالواجب على المكلف أداء ذلك الفعل عيناً، لإمكان الأداء، وحصول موجب التكليف، فإن فات ذلك الواجب بلا تقصير منه لم يأثم ووجب عليه القضاء إن كان له لهذا الواجب خلف، كما قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "من نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فليصلها إذا ذكرها" وإن لم يكن له خلف كصلاة العيدين والجنازة فلا قضاء ولا إثم، وإن قصر في أدائه أثم مطلقاً سواء كان له خلف أم لا وإن لم يكن الفعل مع هذه القدرة مراداً أداء، على غالب ظنه، بل وجب الأداء ليترتب عليه القضاء، أي ليظهر الوجوب في القضاء، فإنه فرع وجوب الأداء وعدمه، ووقت ذلك الفعل الغالب على الظن عدم إمكان أدائه كالأهلية أي وقت صيرورة العبد أهلاً للتكليف في الجزء الأخير من الوقت، فالذي يصير أهلاً للتكليف في الجزء الأخير من وقت الصلاة بحيث لا يسع أدائها، فالصلاة واجبة عليه لكن لا للأداء بل لقضاءها، وهذا مذهب جمهور الحنفية فتجب الصلاة على من أسلم في هذا الجزء، وعلى صبي بلغ، ومجنون أفاق وحائض طهرت فيه. فهذا الوجوب لأجل القضاء، لأن الأداء لا يمكن في ذلك الجزء القليل، فوجوب القضاء على هؤلاء لعجزهم عن الأداء الواجب عليهم بالقدرة الممكنة. خلافاً لزفر لأنه يعتبر لوجوب القضاء إدراك ما يحتمل الأداء من الوقت، فالجزء
Issue: Division of capacity into possible and facilitated. The Hanafis divided the conditioned capacity into possible, explained by soundness of limbs and correctness of means, which is an explanation by necessary concomitant, and into facilitated, which is additional to it as a favor from Him, may He be exalted, with ease. Regarding the first: if the action with this capacity is accompanied by resolve generally, then the obligation is performance adyan (as a matter of personal obligation). Then if it passes without negligence, he does not sin, and making up (qada) is obligatory if there is a substitute; otherwise no qada and no sin. If he was negligent, he sins absolutely. And if performance is not generally possible but is obligatory in order to arrange qada, like the eligibility in the last part of time, it is obligatory contrary to Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) because he considers what the time can accommodate. In al-Tahrir: because there is no certainty about the last part due to possibility of extension. I say: it follows that one cannot be certain of constriction, and sometimes one is certain. Also extension is either by increase of parts, so it expands and no dispute there, or by stretching and expansion, then the statement of a part becomes invalid. Also the real criterion is the last real part, not the last known part. So it is better to say: there is no certainty of the expiry of the last part due to possibility of continuity, and the invalidity of applying the big to such a small might be prevented. All this is debate; the truth is to hold that qada follows either from the obligation itself, as in the case of the sleeper, or from the obligation of a part of performance, as in the case of a transaction that becomes invalid. So reflect. As for the second, the facilitated capacity: obligation is restricted to it, like zakat, for it is a small amount from much property once a year, and therefore it is waived by destruction and nullified by debt. The Hanafis divided the capacity that is a condition of taklif into possible and facilitated. 1. The possible capacity is explained by soundness of limbs and correctness of means, and this is an explanation by necessary concomitant because it is the minimum by which the commanded person can perform what is commanded, whether bodily or financial; and there is no doubt that soundness of limbs and correctness of means are necessary for capacity and evidence of its existence, so they stand in its place in the attachment of rulings upon the responsible person. 2. The facilitated capacity: it is that by which the servant can perform the action with ease, like the conditioned capacity in the obligation of zakat: from growing wealth free of basic needs, upon which a year has passed. Allah made it a condition to add ease as a favor from Him, may He be exalted, upon His servants with ease. The first capacity (possible) is a condition for performing every obligation. But if the performance of the action by this capacity is accompanied by resolve and intention of the action in his predominant opinion, then what is obligatory upon the responsible person is to perform that action adyan, because performance is possible and the cause of obligation obtains. If that obligation passes without negligence from him, he does not sin, and qada is obligatory if this obligation has a substitute, as the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: "Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers." And if it has no substitute, like the prayers of the two 'Ids and the funeral prayer, then no qada and no sin. And if he was negligent in performing it, he sins absolutely, whether it has a substitute or not. And if the action with this capacity is not intended for performance in his predominant opinion, but rather performance is obligatory in order to arrange qada, i.e., to manifest the obligation in qada, for qada is a branch of the obligation of performance and its absence. The time of such an action is one where the predominant opinion is that performance is not possible, like eligibility (i.e., the time when a person becomes eligible for taklif) in the last part of time. Thus, one who becomes eligible for taklif in the last part of the time of prayer such that it does not accommodate its performance: the prayer is obligatory upon him, but not for performance, rather for its qada. This is the position of the majority of Hanafis. Thus prayer is obligatory upon one who accepts Islam in this part, and upon a child who attains puberty, a lunatic who recovers, and a menstruating woman who becomes pure in it. This obligation is for qada, because performance is not possible in that small part. So qada is obligatory upon these persons due to their inability to perform what was obligatory upon them with the possible capacity. Contrary to Zufar, because he considers for the obligation of qada the realization of what can accommodate performance of the time, so the part...
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi exposition of the division of capacity (qudra) into two types: possible (mumkina) and facilitated (muyassara). The first type (possible capacity) is the minimum ability to perform an action, defined by sound limbs and correct means. It is a condition for the obligation of every act. If this capacity is combined with resolve, the act must be performed as a personal duty (adiyan). If missed without negligence, qada is required if there is a substitute (like daily prayers); otherwise no qada or sin. Negligence leads to sin regardless. In certain cases like the last part of time for prayer (when a person becomes responsible just before the time ends), the obligation is not for performance but for qada. This is the majority Hanafi view, opposing Zufar who requires enough time for actual performance. The second type (facilitated capacity) is relevant for obligations like zakat, where ease is considered; it is not strict and is waived if wealth is destroyed or debt exists. The author includes a rebuttal to Zufar's argument and discusses the reasoning about time, concluding that the correct view is that qada follows from the obligation.

Key Terms
القدرة الممكنة (al-qudra al-mumkina): The minimum capacity to perform an act, defined by soundness of limbs and correctness of means; it is a condition for obligation of performance.
القدرة الميسرة (al-qudra al-muyassara): A facilitated capacity that includes ease, e.g., for zakat; obligation is tied to it and falls away if ease is absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, if a person becomes Muslim in the last part of the time for Zuhr prayer such that there is no time to perform it, what is the obligation?
A) The prayer is not obligatory at all.
B) The prayer is obligatory to perform immediately.
C) The prayer is obligatory for qada (make-up), not performance.
D) The prayer is optional.

Key Takeaway
Possible capacity obligates performance and qada; facilitated capacity eases obligation based on ease.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Hanafi Division of Ability and Obligation in the Last Part of Time
Explaining the Hanafi classification of ability as condition for obligation and the ruling for those who become mukallaf at the last moment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between possible ability (al-qudra al-mumkina) and facilitated ability (al-qudra al-muyassara) and apply the Hanafi ruling that qada is wajib for those who become mukallaf in the last part of time, including the dispute with Zufar and the critical refinement of Ibn al-Humam's argument.

Core Idea
Possible ability triggers obligation; if performance is impossible, qada is still wajib because the last part may extend.

This passage from Badakhshani's commentary on Musallam al-Thubut clarifies a key Hanafi usul concept: the division of ability into possible and facilitated. It then applies this to the practical case of a person who becomes legally responsible at the very last moment of prayer time—such a person owes qada even though performance is impossible. You will explore the majority view, Zufar's objection, and Ibn al-Humam's argument about time extension, along with a critical refinement that avoids reliance on miracles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ability
The text defines possible ability (qudra mumkina) as soundness of faculties and validity of causes—the minimum needed to perform any obligation. Facilitated ability (qudra muyassara) adds ease, like the conditions for zakat (productive wealth, year passing, surplus over basic needs).
The Hanafi classification is unique: possible ability is a condition for every wajib, while facilitated ability is a condition for certain obligations like zakat.
2
Understand how possible ability triggers obligation and qada
If a person has possible ability and intends to perform the act, it becomes wajib 'ayn. If missed without negligence and the act has a substitute (like daily prayers), qada is wajib; if negligent, sin is incurred. If the act cannot be performed (e.g., last part of time), the obligation shifts to qada.
Qada is a branch of the obligation of performance; if performance was impossible, qada still becomes wajib because the obligation of performance was established by possible ability.
3
Analyze the dispute between the Hanafi majority and Zufar
The majority hold that qada is wajib for someone who becomes mukallaf (convert, baligh, recovered madman, purified woman) in the last part of prayer time. Zufar argues that since performance was impossible, no obligation of performance existed, so qada cannot be wajib.
The majority rely on the possibility that the last part may extend (e.g., sun slowing) or that the real last part is unknown.
4
Examine the critical refinement of Ibn al-Humam's argument
Ibn al-Humam argued that the last part might extend, citing the miracle of Joshua. The author (Badakhshani) rejects this: Joshua's miracle was for conquest, not prayer, and is a prophetic miracle not analogous. Instead, the better justification is that we cannot be certain the last part has expired—so qada remains wajib.
The author also points out that extending an indivisible part is logically impossible, so the basis is lack of certainty, not actual extension.

قسم الحنفية القدرة التي هي شرط التكليف إلى ممكنة وميسرة .
١ - فالقدرة الممكنة مفسَّرَةٌ (معرفة): بسلامة الآلات وصحة الأسباب، وهو تفسير (تعريف ) باللازم لأنها أدنى ما يتمكن به المأمور من أداء المأمور به بدنياً كان أو مالياً، ولاشك أن سلامة الآلات وصحة الاسباب لازمة للقدرة، ودليل لوجودها فأقيمت مقامها في تعلّق الأحكام.
من
المكلف
-۲ والقدرة الميسَرَةُ : هي التى يتمكن بها العبد من الفعل مع اليسر، كالقدرة المشروطة في إيجاب الزكوة ، من المال النامي الفاضل عن الحوائج الأصلية ، الذي حال عليه الحول شرط الله فيها زيادة اليسر فضلاً منه تعالى على عباده باليسر، والقدرة الأولى ( الممكنة ) شرط لأداء كلّ ،واجب، لكن إن كان إتيان الفعل بسبب هذه القدرة مع العزم وإرادة الفعل في غالب ظنه ، فالواجب على المكلف أداء ذلك الفعل عيناً، لإمكان الأداء، وحصول موجب التكليف ، فإن فات ذلك الواجب بلا تقصير (منه) لم يأثم ووجب عليه القضاء إن كان له لهذا الواجب ) خلف، كما قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه سلّم : " من نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فليصلها إذا ذكرها وإن لم يكن له خلف كصلاة العيدين والجنازة فلا قضاء ولا إثم، وإن قصر في أدائه أثم مطلقاً سواء كان له خلف أم لا وإن لم يكن الفعل مع هذه القدرة مراداً أداء ، على غالب ظنه ، بل وجب الأداء ليترتب عليه القضاء ، أي ليظهر الوجوب في القضاء، فإنه فرع وجوب الأداء وعدمه، ووقت ذلك الفعل الغالب على الظن عدم إمكان أدائه كالأهلية (أي وقت صيرورة العبد أهلاً للتكليف) في الجزء الأخير من الوقت، فالذى يصير أهلاً للتكليف في الجزء الأخير من وقت الصلاة بحيث لا يسع أدائها، فالصلاة واجبة عليه لكن (لا للأداء ) بل لقضاءها ، وهذا مذهب جمهور الحنفية فتجب الصلاة على من أسلم في هذا الجزء ، وعلى صبى بلغ ، ومجنون أفاق وحائض طهرت فيه. فهذا الوجوب لأجل القضاء، لأن الأداء لا يمكن في ذلك الجزء القليل، فوجوب القضاء على هؤلاء لعجزهم عن الأداء الواجب عليهم بالقدرة الممكنة. خلافاً لرفر لأنه يعتبر لوجوب القضاء إدراك ما يحتمل الأداء من الوقت ، فالجزء الأخير لا يحتمل الأداء، فكيف يجب قضاء فعل لم يجب أداءه ؟ فلا يكون القضاء واجباً على هؤلاء عند زفر. وفي " تحرير الأصول" لابن الهمام في الرد على زفر . ( وإنما يجب القضاء على هؤلاء المكلفين في الجزء الأخير من الوقت لأنه لا قطع بكون ذلك الجزء أخيرا لا يمكن فيه الأداء، لإمكان الامتداد، أى امتداد الوقت بابطاء حركة الشمس (هذا) عجيب منه، ولم يمند الوقت للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم غزوة الخندق، فكيف يمتد لكا فر أسلم، أو صبي بلغ أو مجنون أفاق في ذلك الجزء ؟)
ويرة المصنف على كلام صاحب "التحرير" و يقول :
١ أقول: والامتداد ليوشع لم يكن لأجل أداء الصلاة، بل كان لأجل الفتح على الكفار، وثانياً أنه كان معجزة لنبي من أنبياء بني إسرائيل، فلايقاس عليه غيره، وأيضاً يلزم تما في "التحرير" أن لا يقطع ولا يُجزم بالتضييق (تضييق وقت ما لاحتمال الامتداد، وإنما يقطع بتضيق الوقت بسبب قرب الشمس من الأفق طلوعاً أو غروباً. ۲ - وأيضاً قال في الرد على صاحب "التحرير" في صورة احتمال الامتداد: إنه لا يخلو الامتداد عن الحالين : إما يمتد الوقت بازدياد الأجزاء، فيتسع الوقت حينئذ، ولا نزاع فيه ، أو يمتد بالمدو البسط (أى بمد الجزء الأخير و بسطه) و يلزم منه تقسيم الجزء الأخير الذي لا يتجزاء فيلزم منه بطلان قول المتكلمين بوجود الجزء الذى لا يتجزاء ولا ينقسم
٣- وأيضا قال في الرد عليه : إن المناط وما يتعلق به التكليف هو الجزء الأخير الواقعى النفس الأمرى من الوقت ، لا الجزء الأخير الفرضي العلمى الذى نحن نقول إنّه هو الجزء الأخير ، ولا يمتد ما هو جزء أخير واقعي ليس بعده جزء.
فلأولى في توجيه كلام جمهو رالحنفية (من أن وجوب القضاء لأجل وجوب الأداء في الجزء الأخير من الوقت وعدم إمكان الأداء فيه ) أن يقال: لا قطع ، أى لاجزم بانقضاء الجزء الأخير من الوقت لإمكان البقاء ، أى بقاء الجزء الأخير وامتداده ، ولما أورد على هذا القول بأن الفعل الممتد الطويل، كالصلاة، كيف ينطبق على قليل من الوقت وهو الجزء
The Hanafis divided ability, which is a condition of legal obligation, into possible and facilitated. 1- Possible ability is explained (known): by soundness of faculties and validity of causes, and this is an interpretation (definition) by necessary concomitant because it is the minimum by which the commanded person can perform the commanded act, whether bodily or financial. There is no doubt that soundness of faculties and validity of causes are necessary for ability and evidence of its existence, so they are placed in its stead in the attachment of rulings. 2- Facilitated ability: it is that by which the servant can perform the act with ease, like the ability stipulated for the obligation of zakat: from productive wealth surplus to basic needs that has had a year pass. Allah stipulated therein an increase of ease, as a favor from Him upon His servants with ease. The first ability (possible) is a condition for performing every obligation. But if the performance of the act by this ability is with determination and intention to act in his dominant presumption, then the obligated person must perform that act in person, due to the possibility of performance and the occurrence of the cause of obligation. If that obligation is missed without negligence from him, he does not sin and qada is obligatory upon him if this obligation has a substitute, as the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it.' And if it has no substitute, like the Eid prayer and funeral prayer, then no qada and no sin. And if he is negligent in its performance, he sins absolutely, whether it has a substitute or not. And if the act with this ability is not intended for performance in his dominant presumption, rather performance is obligatory so that qada may be consequent upon it, i.e., to manifest the obligation in qada, for it is a branch of the obligation of performance and its absence. And the time of that act where the dominant presumption is inability to perform it, like eligibility (i.e., the time when the servant becomes eligible for obligation) in the last part of time. So the one who becomes eligible for obligation in the last part of prayer time such that it does not accommodate its performance, then the prayer is obligatory upon him, but not for performance, rather for its qada. This is the madhhab of the majority of Hanafis: prayer becomes obligatory on one who accepts Islam in this part, on a child who reaches puberty, a madman who recovers, and a menstruating woman who becomes pure in it. So this obligation is for the sake of qada, because performance is not possible in that small part. So qada is obligatory on these due to their inability to perform the obligation required of them by possible ability. Contrary to Zufar, because he considers for the obligation of qada the realization of that part of time which can accommodate performance. The last part cannot accommodate performance, so how can qada be obligatory for an act whose performance was not obligatory? So qada is not obligatory on these according to Zufar. And in 'Tahrir al-Usul' by Ibn al-Humam in refuting Zufar: (Rather, qada is obligatory on these obligated persons in the last part of time because there is no certainty that that part is the last in which performance is impossible, due to the possibility of extension, i.e., extension of time by slowing of the sun's motion. This is strange from him, and time was not extended for the Prophet ﷺ on the day of the Battle of the Trench, so how can it be extended for an infidel who accepts Islam, a child who reaches puberty, a madman who recovers in that part?) The author comments on the words of the author of al-Tahrir and says: I say: The extension for Joshua was not for the sake of performing prayer, but rather for the conquest over the disbelievers. Secondly, it was a miracle for a prophet from the prophets of the Children of Israel, so others cannot be analogized to him. Also, it follows from what is in al-Tahrir that one should not be certain about the restriction (restriction of time) due to the possibility of extension, but one is certain about the restriction of time due to the proximity of the sun to the horizon at sunrise or sunset. Secondly, he said in refuting the author of al-Tahrir in the case of the possibility of extension: The extension is not free from two states: either the time extends by an increase of parts, then the time becomes wide, and there is no dispute about that; or it extends by elongation and stretching (i.e., by stretching the last part and expanding it), and it would necessitate the division of the last part which is indivisible, which entails the invalidation of the mutakallimun's statement about the existence of the indivisible part that cannot be divided. Thirdly, he said in refutation: The basis and what obligation is attached to is the real last part of time in itself, not the hypothetical scientific last part which we say is the last part, and what is a real last part does not extend because there is no part after it. So the best way to explain the words of the majority of Hanafis (that the obligation of qada is due to the obligation of performance in the last part of time and the impossibility of performance therein) is to say: There is no certainty, i.e., no knowledge, about the expiry of the last part of time due to the possibility of remaining, i.e., the continuation of the last part and its extension. But it was objected to this statement that a long extended act like prayer, how can it fit into a small amount of time which is the part?
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul al-fiqh ruling on the classification of ability (qudra) as a condition for taklif and its application to the case of those who become legally responsible in the last part of prayer time. The author first explains that the Hanafis divide ability into two types: possible ability (al-qudra al-mumkina) and facilitated ability (al-qudra al-muyassara). Possible ability is defined as soundness of faculties and validity of causes; it is the minimum needed to perform an act, and it serves as a condition for all obligations. Facilitated ability includes an additional element of ease, such as in zakat where the wealth must be productive and surplus to basic needs. For possible ability, if the obligated person intends to perform the act, it becomes wajib 'ayn; if missed without negligence, qada is required if there is a substitute (like daily prayers), and if negligent, sin is incurred regardless. However, if the act is not intended for performance, such as when time is too short, the obligation is for qada, not performance. This applies to a convert, a child reaching puberty, a recovered madman, or a menstruating woman who becomes pure in the last part of time. The majority of Hanafis hold that the prayer is wajib for qada. Zufar disagrees, arguing that if performance was impossible, qada cannot be wajib. Ibn al-Humam in 'Tahrir al-Usul' refutes Zufar by suggesting that the last part might extend (like the sun slowing). The author of this work, Badakhshani, criticizes Ibn al-Humam on several points: the analogy to Joshua's miracle is invalid, and the concept of extension of an indivisible part is problematic. Instead, the best explanation is that we cannot be certain that the last part has ended, so qada is still owed. The author defends the majority view without relying on miraculous extension.

Key Terms
القدرة الممكنة (al-qudra al-mumkina): أدنى ما يتمكن به المأمور من أداء المأمور به، وهو سلامة الآلات وصحة الأسباب
القدرة الميسرة (al-qudra al-muyassara): القدرة التي يتمكن بها العبد من الفعل مع اليسر، كشرط إيجاب الزكاة
الجزء الأخير (al-juz' al-akhir): آخر جزء من وقت الصلاة لا يسع أداءها

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafis, what is the ruling on a child who reaches puberty in the last part of Asr time, such that Asr cannot be performed in that time?
A) The Asr prayer is not obligatory at all.
B) The Asr prayer is obligatory to perform immediately in that last part.
C) The Asr prayer is obligatory for qada (make-up) after the time ends.
D) The child must perform a shortened Asr prayer in that time.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, possible ability is sufficient to obligate qada even when performance is impossible, because the last part of time may extend—a principle that leads to the majority ruling that qada is wajib for those who become mukallaf at the last moment.

The Two Types of Ability: Facilitating and Possible
Defining two types of ability conditioning obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between al-qudra al-muyassira and al-qudra al-mumkina and apply the distinction to determine when financial obligations like zakat become binding.

Core Idea
Financial obligations require ease; mere possibility is not enough for zakat.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not all abilities are equal. The capacity to perform an act can be of two kinds: one that merely makes the act possible, and one that makes it easy. This distinction determines when financial acts of worship become obligatory. The passage uses zakat to illustrate how ease (yusr) is a condition for obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of qudra
Locate the terms 'al-qudra al-muyassira' (facilitating ability) and 'al-qudra al-mumkina' (possible ability) in the text. Note how each is defined.
These are technical terms in Hanafi usul.
2
Determine what each conditions
Read carefully: al-qudra al-muyassira conditions 'wujūb al-adā'' (obligation of performance) in financial worship. Al-qudra al-mumkina conditions 'nafs al-wujūb' (the very obligation) itself.
This means that for financial acts, the obligation to perform depends on ease; for others, it depends only on possibility.
3
Examine the zakat example
The text gives zakat as an example where qudra muyassira is required. Identify the indicators of ease: small amount, yearly surplus, and the passing of the year.
These indicators are evidence (dalīl) of ease.
4
Understand the consequence of losing ease
The text mentions that if wealth is destroyed (halak), the obligation of zakat falls. This shows that qudra muyassira is a continuing condition.
If ease disappears, the obligation to perform ceases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثانية (القدرة الميسرة) التي توجب تيسر الأداء على المكلف، فيتقيد بها وجوب الأداء في العبادات المالية، وأما القدرة الممكنة فيتقيد بها نفس الوجوب، كالقدرة على الزكاة، فإن وجوبها مشروط بالقدرة الميسرة، فإن مقدار الواجب في الزكاة شيء قليل من مال كثير في عام بعد حولان الحول، فكل من القلة، واليسر، وبعد حولان الحول، دليل اليسر وعلامة القدرة الميسرة. ولهذا أجل اعتبار اليسر في وجوب الزكاة (سقط وجوب الزكاة بهلاك
As for the second (facilitating ability) which necessitates facilitation of performance for the obligated person, the obligation of performance in financial acts of worship is conditioned by it. As for possible ability, the very obligation is conditioned by it, like the ability for zakat, for its obligation is conditioned by facilitating ability, because the amount of the obligatory [payment] in zakat is a small thing from much wealth in a year after the passing of the year. So each of the smallness, the ease, and the passing of the year is evidence of ease and a sign of facilitating ability. Therefore, consideration of ease in the obligation of zakat (the obligation of zakat falls by destruction...
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage defines two types of qudra (ability) in usul al-fiqh that affect obligation (wujūb). The first is al-qudra al-muyassira (facilitating ability) — this is a form of ability that makes performance easy; it conditions the obligation of performance (wujūb al-adā') in financial acts of worship (ʿibādāt māliyya) like zakat. The second is al-qudra al-mumkina (possible ability) — this conditions the very obligation itself (nafs al-wujūb). The text uses zakat as an example: zakat becomes obligatory only when the helper has facilitating ability, indicated by having a surplus of wealth over a year, with the required payment being small relative to the total. Thus, ease (yusr) is the criterion: if the wealth is lost (halak), the obligation drops because the ability (qudra muyassira) ceases. Note that this distinction is critical in Hanafi usul for understanding when financial obligations like zakat, sadaqat al-fitr, and udhiyah become binding.

Key Terms
القدرة الميسرة (al-qudra al-muyassira): An ability that makes performance easy; it conditions the obligation of performance (wujūb al-adā') in financial worship.
القدرة الممكنة (al-qudra al-mumkina): An ability that merely makes the act possible; it conditions the very obligation (wujūb) itself.
اليسر (al-yusr): Ease; the quality that distinguishes qudra muyassira from mumkina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One applies to prayer, the other to zakat.
B) Al-qudra al-muyassira conditions the obligation of performance (wujūb al-adā') in financial worship, while al-qudra al-mumkina conditions the very obligation (wujūb) itself.
C) Al-qudra al-muyassira is for beginners, al-qudra al-mumkina for advanced.
D) Al-qudra al-muyassira is a temporary ability, al-qudra al-mumkina is permanent.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, financial obligations require facilitating ability (qudra muyassira) that ensures ease; non-financial obligations require only possible ability (qudra mumkina).

Distinguishing the Essence of Obligation from the Obligation of Performance
Resolves a conceptual conflict about sin in delayed wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between nafs al-wujub and wujub al-ada' and apply this distinction to resolve apparent conflicts in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Sin attaches to essence of obligation, not to the obligation of performance.

In Hanafi usul, a key distinction is made between the essence of obligation (nafs al-wujub) and the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada'). This distinction resolves a puzzling scenario: a person who delays a wajib until the last part of its time and dies before making it up is still sinful, even though he did not neglect performance. This lesson unpacks that distinction and demonstrates its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Read the scenario carefully: a wajib (e.g., prayer) becomes due in the last part of its time. The person cannot perform it then and delays qada (make-up) because qada time is expansive, but dies before making it up. The Hanafi ruling says he is sinful. What is the apparent conflict?
Focus on the tension between permissibility of delay and attribution of sin.
2
Understand the Objection
The objector argues: if delaying qada is permissible (ja'iz), how can there be sin? The person was negligent neither in initial performance (impossible) nor in making up (permissible delay). So the objection conflates sin with the act of performance.
The objection assumes sin only arises from a wrongful act or omission.
3
Distinguish the Two Obligations
The author distinguishes between 'essence of obligation' (nafs al-wujub) – the inherent obligatory status of the act – and 'obligation of performance' (wujub al-ada') – the specific duty to perform. Identify how each is defined in the text.
Nafs al-wujub attaches from the moment the act becomes wajib; wujub al-ada' attaches to the act of performing it within time or as qada.
4
Apply the Distinction
Sin (ithm) is based on nafs al-wujub, not wujub al-ada'. Since the act was wajib (nafs al-wujub existed) and the person did not perform it, sin attaches regardless of performance ability. This resolves the problem.
Thus permissibility of delay does not negate sin because sin is on the essence of obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقول : إذا وجب واجب (كالصلاة ) في الجزء الأخير من الوقت وعدمت القدرة في وقت القضاء بأن مات قبل القضاء فالتأثيم لازم على مذهب الحنفية، ولكن هذا مشکل ، لعدم تقصير المكلّف في الاداء؛ لأنه غير مقدور في الجزء الأخير ، وكان تأخير القضاء جائزاً؛ لأن وقته موسع ، ولا تأثيم بالجائز. والجواب عن هذا الإشكال انّ هنا أمرين نفس الوجوب ووجوب الأداء ، ومدار الإثم على نفس الوجوب دون وجوب الأداء، فنفس الوجوب قد وُجد وإن لم يجد وجوب الأداء . فالإثم على نفس الوجوب . والله أعلم بالصواب
I say: When an obligatory act (like prayer) becomes obligatory in the last part of the time, and ability is absent in the time of make-up because he died before making it up, then sin is necessary according to the Hanafi school. But this is problematic, because there is no negligence on the part of the obligated person in performance, since it was not possible in the last part, and delaying the make-up was permissible because its time is expansive, and there is no sin for a permissible act. The answer to this problem is that there are two matters: the essence of obligation and the obligation of performance. The basis of sin is on the essence of obligation, not on the obligation of performance. So the essence of obligation existed even if the obligation of performance did not. So sin is on the essence of obligation. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a problem-solution (ishkal wa jawab) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The problem concerns a person who has an obligatory act like prayer due in the last part of its time but dies before making it up. The Hanafi ruling is that he is sinful. The objection is that he did not delay; the act was not possible in the last part, and delaying qada is permissible because its time is expansive. The solution distinguishes between the essence of obligation (nafs al-wujub) and the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada'). Sin attaches to the essence of obligation, which existed from the beginning, not to performance. Thus the ruling is consistent. The author follows the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
نفس الوجوب (nafs al-wujub): The essence of obligation, the inherent quality of being obligatory that attaches to the act itself regardless of performance.
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada'): The obligation of performance, the specific duty to perform the act within its prescribed time or later.
التأثيم (al-ta'thim): The attribution of sin or legal culpability for failing to fulfill an obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, sin (ithm) is based on which of the following?
A) The obligation of performance (wujub al-ada')
B) The essence of obligation (nafs al-wujub)
C) The ability to perform
D) The permissibility of delay

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, sin (ithm) is attached to the essence of obligation (nafs al-wujub), not the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada').

The Necessity of Understanding for Legal Obligation
Proving necessity of understanding for taklif and refuting objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi/Maturidi condition for taklif and apply the rational proof to refute the opposing view that understanding is not required.

Core Idea
Without understanding the Lawgiver's address, legal obligation is impossible—it would be a request for the unknown.

This lesson examines a foundational principle in Hanafi usul: for a person to be legally obligated (mukallaf), they must understand the Lawgiver's command. The author defends this position against two objections: the case of the drunk person whose divorce is considered valid, and the argument that if the heedless can be obligated, so can animals. We will follow the rational proof and see how the Hanafi school responds to these challenges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on understanding for taklif
Read the text where the author states the condition: 'وشرط التكليف عندنا (الماتريدية) فهم المكلّفِ خطاب الشارع'. Note that this is the Maturidi/Hanafi position. Some Ash'aris who permit taklif of the impossible also agree. Then examine the rational proof that follows.
2
Analyze the rational proof for understanding
The proof (dalil aqli) is: taklif is a request for action; without knowledge of the action, it is a request for the absolute unknown, which is impossible. Therefore, understanding is necessary. Identify the key phrases: 'طلب وقوع الفعل منه' and 'طلب المجهول المطلق'.
3
Address the objection from the drunk person
Opponents cite the drunk person whose divorce etc. are valid despite lack of understanding. The author responds that these rulings are based on linking effects to causes and deterrence, not on full accountability. Also the Quranic verse 'Do not approach prayer while drunk' shows prohibition, not address during drunkenness.
4
Critique the weak evidence from Ibn al-Hajib
The text mentions an argument: if the heedless could be obligated, so could beasts. The author refutes this: even those who permit taklif of the impossible would not automatically extend it to beasts because they deny the conclusion is invalid. This shows the strength of the rational proof over analogical reasoning.

Source Text

I say: It is problematic by the validity of his Islam. The truth is that the drunk person is a respected, obligated person as a deterrent, so his utterances of divorce, manumission, and others are valid, so the rulings are binding on him, except apostasy; due to lack of intent, so it is binding without commitment; giving preponderance to the side of Islam. And the condition of taklif according to us (the Maturidis) is the obligated person's understanding of the address of the Lawgiver. And some of those who permit taklif of the impossible (some Ash'aris) agreed with us on that. And the proof for us is that the taklif of the servant is an expression of requesting the occurrence of the action from him in compliance (by command if it is possible) or trial (by determination to submit if it is a case of taklif of the impossible). And its occurrence from him—i.e., from one who has no perception and awareness of the address—is impossible, because compliance and determination to obey are branches of knowledge of that demanded commanded thing. And because requesting something from a person who does not know that thing is requesting the absolute unknown, which is also impossible. And requesting the impossible is impossible, as passed in the beginning of the third chapter. It was said in objection to this proof: The necessary consequence of this proof is that taklif conditional on lack of understanding is impossible only in the time of understanding, not in the time of lack of understanding, because understanding in the time of lack of understanding is possible; for attention to understanding occurs only in the time of lack of understanding. So taklif of one who does not understand in the time of lack of understanding is not taklif of the impossible, and what is claimed is the invalidity of taklif of one who does not understand in the time of lack of understanding. I say in response: Since it is established that knowledge of the address or the command or the commanded action is among the necessities of the reality of taklif—necessarily, the conception (knowledge) of compliance or trial—so its existence (the existence of taklif) without it, without knowledge, is impossible. And the thing impossible in all times is impossible. So taklif without understanding and knowledge is impossible in the time of lack of understanding, even if understanding is possible during the time of its lack. It is not that the impossibility of taklif depends on the impossibility of understanding, but on its absence. Mention of the weak evidence then the rebuttal. And evidence was adduced (in Mukhtasar Ibn al-Hajib and Tahrir Ibn al-Humam) for the necessity of stipulating understanding for taklif: that if the taklif of the heedless and one who does not understand the address were valid, then the taklif of beasts (horses, mules, donkeys) would be valid, since there is no preventer from taklif of beasts that imagine but do not conceptualize except lack of understanding in beasts. And that is, lack of understanding does not prevent taklif for those who do not stipulate understanding for taklif in humans. So likewise, lack of understanding does not prevent taklif of beasts according to them. It was said regarding the weakness of this evidence: It can be said that this—i.e., the lack of taklif of beasts is due to actual lack of understanding—is denied; rather, perhaps the preventer from taklif of beasts is the lack of aptitude for understanding in them. And there is no dispute about stipulating the aptitude for understanding for taklif, and that aptitude does not exist in beasts. So comparing beasts to those possessed of intellect is an analogy with a difference. I say: The statement of the responder is not valid: "and there is no dispute about stipulating aptitude for understanding"—rather, there is dispute about stipulating aptitude; indeed, those who dispute about stipulating the aptitude for understanding for taklif are those who permit taklif of the impossible, no one else. So taklif of one who has no aptitude is no more remote than taklif of the impossible; they do not prevent permitting taklif of one who has no aptitude. Rather, the truth in refuting that evidence, in agreement with their view (the view of those who permit taklif of the impossible), is to deny the invalidity of the conclusion (the conclusion that if taklif without stipulating understanding is valid then taklif of beasts is valid). So his saying: "Then taklif of beasts would be valid" is the consequence (of 'if') and the consequent of the conditional, and the aspect of its invalidity is that they say taklif of the impossible is permissible, so it is not invalid. Then...
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) discussing the condition of understanding (fahm) for taklif (legal obligation) as held by the Maturidi/Hanafi school. The author begins by addressing an objection concerning the drunk person (sakran): opponents point out that according to Abu Hanifa, the drunk's divorce and ila' are valid, implying he is addressed despite lack of understanding. The author responds that such rulings are based on linking effects to their causes (as fasting is linked to witnessing the moon) and that the drunk is treated as a respected, legally responsible person as a deterrent, so his utterances are valid except apostasy due to lack of intent. The Quranic verse 'Do not approach prayer while drunk' is then cited; the author argues it does not prove that the drunk cannot understand the address, but rather shows prohibition during drunkenness. The core of the passage then states the Maturidi condition: the obligated person must understand the Lawgiver's address. Some Ash'aris agree. The rational proof (dalil aqli) is presented: taklif is a request for an action from a person; if the person has no knowledge of the action, it is a request for the absolute unknown, which is impossible. Obedience requires knowledge of what is commanded. An objection is raised that the impossibility only pertains to the time when understanding is absent, but understanding in that time is possible, so taklif is not impossible. The author refutes this by explaining that knowledge is a necessity of taklif; without it, taklif is impossible in all times. The passage then mentions weak evidence from Ibn al-Hajib and Ibn al-Humam: if the heedless could be obligated, so could beasts, since the only preventer is lack of understanding. A rebuttal claims the preventer is lack of aptitude for understanding, and there is no dispute about that. The author corrects this: there is dispute; those who permit taklif of the impossible do not require aptitude. The correct refutation is to deny that the conclusion (taklif of beasts) is automatically invalid, because those who permit impossible taklif would not find it absurd. Thus the passage underscores that understanding is essential for valid taklif according to the Hanafi/Maturidi position.

Key Terms
التكليف (al-taklif): Legal imposition or obligation, defined as requesting the occurrence of an action from a person in compliance or trial.
الفهم (al-fahm): Understanding or comprehension of the address of the Lawgiver, considered a condition for valid taklif.
السكران (al-sakran): The drunk person; considered legally responsible (mukallaf) for certain rulings like divorce and manumission as a deterrent, but not for apostasy due to lack of intent.
الاستعداد (al-isti'dad): Aptitude or preparedness for understanding; distinguishes humans from animals in terms of potential for taklif.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi/Maturidi position in this passage, what is the essential condition for taklif (legal obligation)?
A) The obligated person must be completely free from sin.
B) The obligated person must understand the address of the Lawgiver.
C) The obligated person must be a male adult.
D) The obligated person must have performed Hajj at least once.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi/Maturidi usul, understanding the Lawgiver's address is a rationally necessary condition for valid legal obligation; without it, taklif is impossible.

The Legal Capacity of an Intoxicated Person: Hanafi Distinctions
Critical refinement of the drunk person's capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a drunk person's divorce is valid but his apostasy is not, and identify the Qur'anic and Hadith evidence used to support this distinction.

Core Idea
The drunk person has partial capacity: utterances harming others are binding, but apostasy requires genuine intention.

This passage tackles a critical usul al-fiqh question: is a person who becomes intoxicated from a prohibited act fully responsible for his statements? The Hanafi school does not give a blanket answer; instead, it distinguishes between actions that affect others' rights (like divorce, manumission, and property damage) and those requiring sincere conviction (like apostasy). The author engages with an opposing view that cites Qur'an 4:43 to argue for full accountability, and provides a nuanced textual analysis that preserves both deterrence and the integrity of religious commitment.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the capacity of the drunk person
Identify the acts for which the drunk person is considered responsible (divorce, zihar, compensation) and the one act that is not valid (apostasy). Note the reason: deterrence for harmful acts but lack of intention for apostasy.
The principle: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' — intention matters, but deterrence overrides in cases of harm.
2
Analyze the opposing argument from Qur'an 4:43
The opponents claim that because the verse commands the drunk to refrain from prayer, he is addressed and therefore fully accountable. Write down the verse and the opponent's inference.
Verse: 'Do not approach prayer while you are drunk until you know what you are saying.'
3
Deconstruct the Hanafi response to the verse
The author distinguishes between general understanding (which the drunk retains) and certainty (yaqin) required for full responsibility. The phrase 'until you know' is interpreted as 'until you are certain' — a higher epistemic standard. Note that Abu Hanifa's definition of intoxication for punishment is precautionary, not a denial of all understanding.
The hadith 'Avert hudud by doubts' supports the precautionary approach.
4
Examine the role of intention in apostasy
Apostasy requires a deliberate choice to leave Islam and embrace disbelief. In drunkenness, the person lacks sound intention; the utterance of disbelief is involuntary. The author distinguishes between 'occurrence' (luzum) of the words and actual adoption of disbelief.
This shows that not all utterances by a drunk are treated equally.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi view, a drunk's divorce is valid and binding, but his apostasy is not. Under the opposing view, both might be valid or invalid. Understand how this difference affects legal rulings in practice.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different interpretations of the same textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحق في الجواب عن إشكال السكران أن السكران إذ كان سكره من فعل محرم فهو مكلف زجراً باعتبار طلاقه وإيلائه، ووجوب الغرامة عليه بإتلاف مال أحد. فتصح عباراته من الطلاق والعتاق وغيرهما، فلزمه الإحكام، إلا ردته؛ فإنها لا تعتبر لعدم القصد، إذ الردة تكون بقصد ترك الإسلام واختيار الكفر، وليس له في حال السكر قصد وإرادة صحيحة، فكأنه (اختيار الردة) لروم الكفر عليه من غير اختيار دون التزام الكفر (ولزوم الكفر ليس بكفر) وإنما يكون في ردته لزوم، دون الالتزام ترجيحاً لجانب الإسلام.
٢- وقالوا ثانياً : قال الله تعالى : (لا تقربوا الصلاة وأنتم سكارى) فكلفوا في حال السكر بترك الصلاة، فعلم أن السكران مكلف.
أقول في الجواب عن استدلالهم هذا: ليس فيه دليل على كون السكران مكلفاً مع عدم فهم الخطاب، بل فيه دليل على أن السكر لا ينافي فهم الخطاب في الجملة (في بعض الأمور) كما يقتضيه (الفهم في الجملة) حد السكران وتعريفه باختلاط الكلام والهذيان أي علامة السكران هذان الأمران، واعتبار الإمام أبي حنيفة عدم التميز بين الأشياء في تعريف السكر الموجب للحد والعقوبة احتياط منه، وليس هذا نفي الفهم في الجملة، لأن الحد على الدرء والدفع شرعاً، وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: "ادرءوا الحدود بالشبهات" حديث معروف. ومعنى الآية اللاحقة حتى تعلموا ما تقولون أي حتى تيقنوا ما تقولون، فإن في حال السكر لا يبين بما يقول، بل يحصل له مجرد الظن، فالسكر مبني على اليقين الذي يحصل في نهاية الفهم، ولا ينافي الفهم الذي لابد منه في توجه الخطاب. وهذا الذي ذكرنا في مفهوم حتى تعلموا ليس بتأويل، بل هو تفسير، فإن العلم المذكور في الآية هو اليقين، وإلا فنفس الظن حاصل لهم، ومن أجل ذلك يختلطون في كلامهم. وأما القوم كابن الحاجب وابن الهمام وغيرهما فقد التزموا التأويل في هذه الآية، وقالوا بأنها نهي عن السكر، أي لا تقربوا المسكر، أو لا تشرب مسكراً فتقربوا الصلاة سكرانا، والحال أنكم تصلون، فلا تعلمون ما تقولون كقولهم: "لا تمت وأنت ظالم أي لا تظلم فتموت ظالماً". خذ هذا .
The truth in answering the problem of the drunken person is that the drunken person, when his drunkenness results from a prohibited act, is legally responsible as a deterrent regarding his divorce and his oath of zihar, and the obligation of compensation for destroying someone's property. Thus his utterances of divorce, manumission, and others are valid, so the rulings take effect upon him, except for his apostasy; it is not considered due to lack of intent. For apostasy occurs with the intent to leave Islam and choose disbelief, and he has no intent or sound will in a state of drunkenness. So it is as if (choosing apostasy) due to the inclination towards disbelief occurring to him involuntarily without adopting disbelief. (And the occurrence of disbelief is not disbelief.) Rather, in his apostasy there is occurrence, not adoption, giving preference to the side of Islam.
2- Secondly, they said: Allah Almighty said: 'Do not approach prayer while you are drunk.' So they were obliged in a state of drunkenness to refrain from prayer; thus it is known that the drunken person is legally responsible.
I say in response to this argument: It does not contain proof that the drunken person is legally responsible while not understanding the address. Rather, it contains proof that drunkenness does not negate understanding the address in general (in some matters). As the definition of a drunken person requires understanding in general, his definition is confusion of speech and delirium. These two matters are signs of the drunken person. Abu Hanifa's consideration of lack of discrimination between things in defining drunkenness that necessitates the prescribed punishment is a precaution from him. This is not a negation of understanding in general, because prescribed punishment is based on repulsion and prevention by law. His statement, peace be upon him: 'Avert prescribed punishments by doubts' is a well-known hadith. The meaning of the subsequent verse 'until you know what you are saying' is 'until you are certain of what you are saying.' For in a state of drunkenness, he does not clarify what he says; rather, he merely obtains conjecture. So drunkenness is based on certainty that occurs at the end of understanding, and it does not negate the understanding necessary for the address to be directed. This which we mentioned regarding the meaning of 'until you know' is not interpretation but exegesis. For the knowledge mentioned in the verse is certainty. Otherwise, they would have mere conjecture, and because of that they become confused in their speech. As for the people like Ibn al-Hajib, Ibn al-Humam, and others, they committed to interpretation of this verse and said it is a prohibition of drinking, i.e., 'Do not approach intoxicants' or 'Do not drink an intoxicant and approach prayer while drunk, while you are praying, so you do not know what you are saying,' like their saying: 'Do not die while you are an oppressor,' i.e., 'Do not oppress and die an oppressor.' Take this.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul dispute about the legal capacity (taklif) of an intoxicated person (sukran). The author, from the Hanafi perspective, addresses two main objections raised by opponents who claim that the drunken person is fully accountable (mukallaf). 

The author first clarifies the Hanafi position: if a person becomes drunk from a prohibited act (e.g., drinking alcohol), he remains legally responsible for actions that involve harming others, such as pronouncing divorce, making an oath of zihar (a form of divorce-like prohibition), and destroying property. His utterances in these matters are valid and binding. However, his apostasy (riddah) is not considered valid because apostasy requires a genuine intention to leave Islam and choose disbelief. In a state of drunkenness, he lacks proper intent and will; the inclination towards disbelief occurs to him involuntarily. Therefore, the occurrence (luzum) of the words of disbelief is not actual disbelief (kufr) because intention is absent.

The second objection cites the Qur'anic verse (4:43): 'Do not approach prayer while you are drunk.' The opponents argue that this verse obliges the drunken person to refrain from prayer, implying he is addressed and thus responsible. The author refutes this by distinguishing between general understanding (fahm al-khitab) and the specific nuance of the verse. He argues that drunkenness does not negate understanding in general; the definition of a drunken person includes confusion of speech and delirium, which indicates partial comprehension. Abu Hanifa's definition of drunkenness for the purpose of prescribed punishment (hadd) is based on lack of discrimination as a precautionary measure (ihtiyat), not a denial of all understanding. The Prophet's hadith 'Avert prescribed punishments by doubts' supports this. The verse 'until you know what you are saying' is interpreted as 'until you are certain (yaqin)' not just any knowledge. The drunken person may have conjecture (zann) but not certainty, which is required for full legal address. The author insists this is exegesis (tafsir), not interpretive distortion (ta'wil). He notes that scholars like Ibn al-Hajib and Ibn al-Humam took the verse as a prohibition of drinking itself, but the author distinguishes his approach.

This lesson guards against the misunderstanding that a drunken person is either completely unaccountable or completely accountable. The Hanafi position is nuanced: he is accountable for harmful, prohibited acts that affect others out of deterrence (zajran), but not for apostasy which requires sound intention.

Key Terms
سكران (sukran): A person in a state of intoxication, defined by confusion of speech and delirium, but not necessarily total loss of understanding.
مكلف (mukallaf): A person addressed by divine law (shar') and held responsible for his actions.
ردة (riddah): Apostasy from Islam, which requires intentional choice and rejection of faith; not considered valid when uttered without intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on the apostasy (riddah) of a person who became intoxicated from a prohibited drink?
A) It is valid and he becomes an apostate.
B) It is invalid because he lacks the intention required for apostasy.
C) It is valid only if he repeated it three times.
D) It is suspended until he becomes sober.

Key Takeaway
The intoxicated person has partial legal responsibility: his harmful utterances are valid, but acts requiring sincere intention (like apostasy) are not.

The Obligation of Non-Existent Beings (Taklif al-Ma'dum)
Defending the Hanafi view that non-existent beings can be addressed conceptually

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on taklif al-ma'dum, distinguish between conceptual (aqli) and actual (tanjizi) attachment, apply the analogy of the messenger's command, and evaluate the Mu'tazili objection and Ibn al-Qattan's compromise.

Core Idea
Hanafi: non-existent beings are obligated conceptually via Allah's eternal knowledge, not actually.

This lesson explores a key theological and usul dispute: can Allah's eternal command address non-existent beings? The Hanafi school affirms this in a conceptual sense to preserve the eternity of Allah's speech, while the Mu'tazila object that it implies futility. The text also critiques a compromise by Ibn al-Qattan, an Ash'ari scholar, who claimed that only a generic eternal speech exists and that specific commands are temporal. Understanding this debate sharpens your grasp of the nature of Allah's speech (kalam nafsi) and how commands relate to their subjects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the Hanafi position
First, determine the core question: can a non-existent being be obligated (mukallaf)? The Hanafi answer is yes, but only in a conceptual sense (taliq 'aqli), not an actual one (tanjizi). The text begins 'المعدوم مكلف خلافاً للمعتزلة'.
The distinction 'taliq 'aqli' vs 'tanjizi' is crucial.
2
Analyze the Mu'tazili objection
Next, state the opponent's argument: if Allah commands non-existent beings, it is foolish (safah) and pointless (abath) because there is no actual object to receive the command. The text says 'قالوا: يلزم أمر ونهي من غير متعلق موجود، وذلك سفه وعبث'.
This objection targets the idea that the command must be addressed to an existent entity.
3
Examine the Hanafi response: conceptual vs actual attachment
The Hanafi response refutes the objection by distinguishing temporal actuality from eternal conceptual relation. The command in eternity is a conceptual demand based on Allah's knowledge that the addressee will exist, analogous to a messenger's command that applies to people not yet born. The text: 'والمراد التعلق العقلى، لا التنجيزى ... كأمر الرسول في حقنا'.
The analogy (qiyas) with the messenger's command shows that commands can apply to those who do not exist at the time of issuance.
4
Critically evaluate Ibn al-Qattan's compromise
Ibn al-Qattan (an Ash'ari) attempted to avoid the problem by positing that Allah's eternal speech is a generic common element (al-amr al-mushtarak), and specific commands are temporal accidents. The author refutes this by arguing that a genus cannot exist without a species, and if the divisions are merely accidents, the eternal element would be unintelligibly bare. Thus, his position falls into inconsistency.
The critique uses logical reasoning: genus/species and accident/substance.
5
Conclude with the tarjih (preferred view)
The author supports the Hanafi position as sound, having refuted both the Mu'tazili objection and Ibn al-Qattan's alternative. The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that Allah's speech remains eternal and the taklif of non-existent beings is valid conceptually.
This upholds the Hanafi-Ash'ari doctrine of kalam nafsi as eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة تكليف المعدومين حين نزول التكليف المعدوم مكلف خلافاً للمعتزلة، والمراد التعلق العقلى، لا التنجيزى لنا وإلا لم يكن التكليف أزلياً؛ لتوقفه على التعلق، وهو أزلى؛ لأن كلامه أزلى، لامتناع قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى، وفيه مافيه، قالوا: يلزم أمر ونهي من غير متعلق موجود، وذلك سفه وعبث، قلنا : إنما يلزم ذلك لوكان الطلب في الأزل تنجيزاً، وأما لوكان ممن سيكون فلا، كأمر الرسول في حقنا وبذلك اندفع ماقيل: إن تحقق التعلق بدون المتعلق ممتنع، ضرورة أن الإضافة لا يتحقق بدون المضاف إليه، وذلك لأن الامتناع في التعلق التنجيزى، وأما العقلى فيكفي له العلم، فتدبر قيل: السفه والبعث من صفات الأفعال والكلام النفسى من الصفات فلا يتصف بهما أقول: الأمر طلب، والطلب يتصف بهما إجماعاً اعلم أن عبد الله بن سعيد بن القطان من الأشاعرة ذهب مستخلصاً عن اللزوم إلى أن كلامه تعالى ليس في الأزل أمراً ونهيا أو غيرهما، بل القديم هو الأمر المشترك، والأقسام حادثة أورد عليه أن هذه أنواع ويستحيل وجود الجنس إلا في ضمن نوع ما وأجاب بمنع أنها أنواعه، بل عوارضه بحسب التعلق، ويجوز خلوه عنه أقول : وجود المقيم بدون وجود قسم ما محال، وإن كان التقسيم باعتبار العوارض فيلزم عليه القول بوجود قسم ما بدون هذه العوارض وهو لا يعقل، مع أنه قال: إن القديم هو المشترك هذا خلف، فتدبر وأيضاً لا يكون المعدوم حينئذ مكلفاً؛ إذ لا تعلق، قالوا: يلزم قدم عدم التناهى، فإن المتعلق بزيد غير المتعلق بعمرو
Issue: The obligation of non-existent beings at the time of revelation. The non-existent being is obligated, contrary to the Mu'tazila. What is intended is conceptual (aqli) attachment, not actual (tanjizi) for us. Otherwise, obligation would not be eternal, because it depends on attachment, and it is eternal because His speech is eternal, due to the impossibility of temporal accidents subsisting in His essence, may He be exalted. There is something in it. They said: It necessitates command and prohibition without an existing object of attachment, and that is foolishness and senselessness. We say: That would only be necessary if the demand in eternity was actual (tanjizi). If it is for one who will exist, then no, like the command of the messenger in our right. And with that, what was said is refuted: that actualization of attachment without the object of attachment is impossible, necessarily because the relation cannot be actualized without the term of the relation. That is because impossibility is in actual attachment. As for conceptual, knowledge suffices for it. So reflect. It was said: Foolishness and sending are attributes of actions, and internal speech is among the attributes, so it cannot be described by them. I say: Command is a demand, and demand is described by both by consensus. Know that Abdullah ibn Saeed ibn al-Qattan, from the Ash'aris, went freeing from the necessity to the position that His speech, may He be exalted, is not from eternity command or prohibition or others; rather, the eternal is the common element, and the divisions are temporal. It was objected to him that these are types, and the genus cannot exist except within a type. He answered by denying that they are types; rather, they are accidents of it according to attachment, and it is possible for it to be without them. I say: The existence of the permanent without any division is impossible. Even if the division is based on accidents, it necessarily follows the statement of the existence of some division without these accidents, which is unintelligible. Moreover, he said that the eternal is the common element; this is inconsistency. So reflect. Also, the non-existent would not then be obligated, since there is no attachment. They said: It necessitates the pre-eternity of non-finiteness, because the attachment to Zayd is different from the attachment to Amr.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul dispute concerning whether non-existent beings (ma'dumun) can be addressed by Allah's eternal command (taklif). The Hanafi position holds that at the time of revelation, non-existent individuals are obligated in a conceptual sense (taliq 'aqli), not an actual, applied sense (tanjizi). This is necessary to preserve the eternity of Allah's speech, which cannot be temporally conditioned. 

The author first states the issue and the Hanafi view, then addresses the Mu'tazili objection: if Allah commanded non-existent beings, it would be foolish (safah) and pointless (abath) because there is no actual object. The Hanafi response distinguishes between eternal demand (al-talb fi al-azal) as a conceptual relation: the command is for those who will exist, not for an actually present object. This is analogous to the command of a messenger that applies to us after his time. 

The objection that a relation (idafa) requires both terms is refuted: actual relation requires the object, but conceptual relation only requires knowledge (al-'ilm). The author then critiques the position of Ibn al-Qattan, an Ash'ari scholar, who tried to avoid the problem by saying Allah's eternal speech is a common undifferentiated element (al-amr al-mushtarak), and specific commands and prohibitions are temporal accidents (awarid). The first objection: genus cannot exist without some type. Ibn al-Qattan responded that the divisions are not types but accidents. The author finds this inconsistent: if eternal speech is a common element, it must have some division, and if it is undifferentiated, it cannot be described as command or prohibition. Also, if the divisions are only accidents, then the eternal essence would exist without any division, which is unintelligible. Thus, the non-existent would not be obligated because there is no attachment. Finally, the author notes that if attachments to different individuals are different, it implies infinite pre-eternity (qidam 'adam al-tanahi), which is problematic.

This lesson guards against misunderstanding the Hanafi view as claiming actual obligation of non-existent beings; it is conceptual (taliq 'aqli) based on Allah's eternal knowledge.

Key Terms
معدوم (ma'dum): A non-existent being, considered as the object of a hypothetical obligation in eternity.
تعلق عقلي (taliq 'aqli): Conceptual attachment of a command to a subject based on knowledge of future existence, not actual presence.
كلام نفسي (kalam nafsi): Internal, eternal speech of Allah as an attribute, not composed of letters and sounds.
أمر مشترك (amr mushtarak): A common undifferentiated element; Ibn al-Qattan's term for the eternal speech before specification into commands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what kind of attachment (taliq) does Allah's eternal obligation have to non-existent beings?
A) Actual attachment (taliq tanjizi)
B) Conceptual attachment (taliq 'aqli)
C) No attachment whatsoever
D) Attachment based on the existence of the object at that time

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi view on taklif al-ma'dum is a conceptual (aqli) attachment based on Allah's eternal knowledge, preserving the eternity of His speech while avoiding irrationality.
